Japan's Sporting Ambition: Aiming to Host the Olympics in Ten Years 111

According to a Dongbao Telegraphic dispatch, the Japanese student track and field team, which is on a European tour, arrived in Stockholm on July 26 and was welcomed by Mr. Aidosto Rom, President of the International Amateur Athletic Federation. Japan Builds Large Swimming Pool 112

Raising 250,000 Gold

Remodeling the Meiji Jingu Swimming Pool

--To Be Completed by Next Summer--

(Special Correspondent) The Meiji Jingu swimming pool in Tokyo was hastily built for temporary use during the Far Eastern Games, and its facilities were inadequate. In order to renovate it according to the original ideal plan, Chairman Suehiro has been running around, but he has only been able to raise 30,000 yuan. At a time when he was in despair, he suddenly received the efforts of Dr. An Qingyi, Chairman of the Taixie Association, who secured a generous donation of 150,000 yuan from the Harada Accumulation Association. However, the lowest budget for construction is 250,000 yuan. It has been decided to start construction in October to rebuild the ideal facilities. The current grandstand only holds 8,000 people, and it will be expanded to accommodate 15,000 people. The main grandstand will be made of reinforced concrete with medical, administrative, and bathing facilities built underneath. There will also be 1,500 new-style steel clothing racks for men and women. In addition, electric lighting will be installed on the water surface, and wells will be dug to replace the water in the swimming pool. The project is expected to be completed next summer and will be the largest and most well-equipped swimming pool in the Orient.

Five Groups Competed

Turning defeat into victory. The battle between Shen Yongnian and Wang Wuchen was believed by observers to be certain victory for Shen. The result was unexpected. The score was one to six. In the second set, Shen seemed to have the intention of letting Wang make three games first, and then chasing up to equality. Shen used all his strength to recover, with the battle reaching its climax. In the eleventh and twelfth games, Shen seemed flustered and made mistakes, losing the whole game with a score of five to seven. Although Wang was covered in sweat in the third set, his spirits were doubled, and the power of his shots was also stronger than before. Every morning at five o'clock, he walked from his residence in Zhabei to the public sports field to practice, regardless of the cold or heat, for two years without interruption. His ability to fight for a long time without fatigue and turn defeat into victory was not accidental.

Sun Chuanxin is young and thin, and his history of practicing tennis is very short. The two fought vigorously at six o'clock yesterday morning. His opponent, Xu Qiaosheng, is also like that. The two warm waters just became a pair. It takes a dozen back and forth to determine the victory or defeat of a ball. It can also be seen in his conservative work. As a result, Xu Qiaosheng won with a score of 6-4, 6-1.

The short-legged tiger meets the long man. Zhang Quansheng is very short and his skills are improving very quickly. He can attack and defend and is one of the bullies in the ball group. So his friends call him the short-legged tiger. Yesterday, he fought against Yang Shiqing, who is very tall. The confrontation between the north and the south is interesting. Although the tiger is fierce, the long man also has a long strength. After a long battle, the victory was decided. The god of victory abandoned people and took the tiger. The score was 6-4, 8-6.

Local News

Slight Disturbances in the Foreign Concessions Yesterday 116

The Chinese Areas Remained Quiet

The city implemented strict precautions yesterday. From 12:00 midnight the night before, Nanshi and Zhabei announced martial law and cut off traffic. The police departments of the British and French Concessions also implemented strict precautions. Therefore, except for slight disturbances in the Nanjing Road and North Sichuan Road areas of the Public Concession, no major incidents occurred yesterday.

In the Public Concession, around 9:30 yesterday morning, many men and women resembling workers and students gradually gathered in the area of Nanjing Road and Tibet Road. A shout was heard and leaflets were scattered, mixed with the sound of firecrackers, creating a very chaotic scene. The Laozha police station, which was in charge of the area, was already on alert, and Chinese and Western armed patrolmen immediately stepped forward to arrest the crowd. The crowd was dispersed, and the remaining crowd fled east along Lloyd Road and Zhejiang Road. Shops on both sides temporarily closed their doors to prevent accidents. The patrolmen chased after them and arrested eight people, who were sent to the police car parked on the road. Seeing that the situation was not good, the crowd scattered in groups of three or five and fled. At the intersection of Shanxi Road and Nanjing Road, three people were arrested by patrolmen from the Central Police Station. A police car was also parked at the intersection of Henan Road and Nanjing Road, and many armed patrolmen were on guard. Seeing the precautions, the crowd flocked to Sichuan Road and the Bund. However, the more radical ones still threw bricks and stones at the glass windows of shops when passing the intersection of Nanjing Road and Henan Road. The Chinese and Western detectives on guard stepped forward to disperse them. Although they did not succeed in their attempts, one or two places were damaged. The crowd then turned into Sichuan Road and headed east towards the Bund, passing over the Baidu Bridge and along North Suzhou Road towards Hongkou. The leaflets in their hands were no longer numerous, and they only shouted slogans along the way. Seven people were arrested in the Hongkou area, four of whom were released because they were not involved. Near Haining Road on North Sichuan Road, some people resembling workers were also found in the morning. However, the number was still small and they only threw leaflets into the trams. Around 11:00 in the morning, those found on the road were mostly from Nanjing Road and the Bund, but they no longer took any action.

In the French Concession, around 3:00 AM and 9:00 AM yesterday, leaflets were secretly distributed in areas such as Rue Massenet, Rue Paul Henry, and Route des Pères. By the time the detectives arrived, they had already fled without a trace. The Great World Amusement Park, which usually opens after 12:00 PM every day, was delayed until 2:35 PM yesterday before ticket sales began. At 5:30 PM, due to the large number of pedestrians in the area, the police station was notified to temporarily close the park until 8:10 PM, when it returned to normal.

In the Chinese areas of Nanshi, Zhabei, Xujiahui, Longhua, and Caojiadu, strict precautions were taken. All the key points were guarded by the Public Security Bureau with double posts armed with guns, which was very thorough. Pedestrians and vehicles that were slightly suspicious were checked. Soldiers were guarding at the Zhabei New Gate Bridge and the Hengfeng Road Bridge, and the situation was serious. From 12:00 midnight, the same measures as the night before were taken, with martial law implemented and vehicles and pedestrians prohibited from passing.

Military and Political Authorities Strictly Prohibit Unauthorized Strikes 117

Labor-Management Disputes Should Be Handled in Accordance with Legal Procedures

A joint proclamation from the Songhu Garrison Command and the Shanghai Municipal Government stated: Regarding the fact that labor-management disputes in industry and commerce must be submitted to the competent authorities for mediation or arbitration in accordance with legal procedures, and strikes must not be carried out without authorization, proclamations have been issued and strictly prohibited in the past. It is now reported that there are unscrupulous people who are inciting strikes. At this time when the punitive military operations are progressing, the defense of the rear is of utmost importance and prohibitions should be reiterated and precautionary measures be taken. Any enterprise where a labor dispute occurs must first submit to the competent authorities for mediation or arbitration in accordance with the law and must not use strikes as a threat. Those who engage in unauthorized strikes without going through the mediation or arbitration process will be prosecuted by the military and police organs for disturbing public order and will not be treated with leniency. All must comply and not disobey. This is the proclamation.

Postal Service Dispute Negotiations 118

Talks Between Both Sides Still Yield No Results

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Employees' Union previously submitted ten consolidated demands regarding long-standing issues to the postal authorities, setting a five-day deadline for a response, as reported in previous issues. It has now come to light that, with the deadline passed and no response from the authorities, the two unions sent representatives Zhu Xuefan, Zhang Kechang, and employee representatives Chuan Dewei, Chen Lingzhou, Kang Yong, and Shi Ji Kuan, seven in total, to the Postal Commissioner's Office for a meeting to ascertain the authorities' sincerity in providing a satisfactory response. Commissioner Wei Yifu was unable to come to Shanghai due to pressing matters at the Ministry of Transportation, so the union representatives were received by Yang Sili, secretary of the Commissioner's Office. After two rounds of talks, Secretary Yang conveyed the authorities' opinions to the representatives. The authorities indicated that they could accept or amend the following seven of the ten demands raised by the union: (1) revisions to the regulations for short, long, and sick leave, as well as new regulations for marriage, mourning, and regular leave for Chinese postal staff; (3) abolishing the messenger boy certificate and thoroughly improving their treatment; (6) restoring the "Personnel History" semi-monthly publication; (7) correcting General Bureau Order No. 208 regarding the Postal Commissioner's secretary enjoying the same treatment as postal staff; (8) stipulating that letter carriers injured on duty or elderly should become in-house letter carriers; (9) explicitly stipulating that letter carriers or messengers who have served for more than fifteen years can be promoted to postal assistants after a simple examination. Regarding (2) subsidies for the high cost of gold and low value of silver (an increase of one-eighth per month) and (10) improvements to the year-end bonus (employees with more than one year of service receive a bonus of one and a half months), the authorities indicated that they could not accept these because the total salaries of postal personnel nationwide amounted to 17 million yuan. An increase of one-eighth per month would require more than 2 million yuan, and a year-end bonus based on one and a half months would require 400,000 yuan. The union representatives also refused to concede. The talks over the past two days have yielded no results, as both sides remained firm in their positions. Furthermore, regarding (4) open finances, the authorities indicated that they could be open, but the union representatives were not satisfied with their so-called openness. The union believes that the separation of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau from the post office effectively absorbs the post office's cash, harming the post office's future. Therefore, the union's true intention in advocating for open postal finances is to merge the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau back into the post office. This issue was also a focal point of contention between the two sides. Yesterday afternoon, the talks broke down and the meeting adjourned without any resolution.

One: Denouncing the Bogus Beiping Central Enlarged Conference - No Legal Basis, Tracing the Collusion of Traitors Yan and Feng, and the Western Hills Faction's Reorganization into a Putrid Enlarged Conference in the Style of the Chau An Society. There is absolutely no legal basis. Is the so-called Central Enlarged Conference based on any particular Central Committee? What is this so-called enlargement?

Two: The Meeting's Situation Is Ridiculous. This farce is laughable. It is claimed that there are more than 30 people, but only 11 attended, and one person signed for three people. What value does this have? The very first gathering has formed such a self-deceiving situation. The peculiarities and ridiculousness of subsequent scenes are even more laughable. National Anti-Smuggling Conference Convened Yesterday 120

A Total of Twenty-Eight Representatives Attended

Salt Commissioner Zou Lin Gave a Speech on Behalf of Song

The National Anti-Smuggling Conference, organized by the Ministry of Finance, held its opening ceremony at the Xieqiao Anti-Smuggling Office at 2 p.m. yesterday. In addition to the representatives from various bureaus mentioned in yesterday's report, those who arrived temporarily included Hu Mingzao, head of the Anti-Smuggling Special Task Force stationed in Songjiang, Li Di, representative of the Northern Anhui Anti-Smuggling Bureau, and Huang Xiancheng, chief of the Secretariat Section and above of the Anti-Smuggling Office, totaling twenty-eight people. As Anti-Smuggling Commissioner Wen Yingxing was in Beijing and had not returned, Deputy Commissioner Ke Sen represented Chairman Song Ziwen and appointed Salt Commissioner Zou Lin to attend and give instructions. After the opening ceremony, the attendees performed the required rituals. First, the chairman delivered an opening speech, stating in part: "Today's Anti-Smuggling Conference is the first meeting convened since the establishment of this office. The purpose of the meeting is to rectify anti-smuggling efforts by gathering the wisdom and talents of many people to plan the rectification of anti-smuggling. This conference is extremely important for the future of anti-smuggling. Although the abuses in anti-smuggling are deeply ingrained, advocating for rectification is not something new. However, if we want to thoroughly eliminate them, it cannot be achieved overnight. If we do not get to the root of the problem, identify the crux of the matter, and apply systematic and planned remedies, then simply talking about rectification will be useless. Therefore, before convening this conference, we sent inspectors from this office to various bureaus to conduct thorough investigations to clarify the truth. We also ordered each bureau to examine the local situation, formulate plans for rectification, submit them for discussion, and organize a preparatory office for the Anti-Smuggling Conference to compile and review various proposals to ensure thoroughness. All these procedures are intended to ensure that the discussions at this conference are practical and not just empty talk. Since the establishment of this office, six months have passed. During these six months, the fundamental plans for rectifying anti-smuggling have been put into practice. I would like to report the following matters to everyone present: revising the regulations to unify authority, training special task forces to strengthen our forces, and establishing training schools to cultivate talent. There are many other things that are waiting to be implemented. Now, I am delighted that everyone has come to the meeting to share their usual experiences and knowledge to discuss and plan the way forward. I hope that everyone present will carefully study the proposals of this office and various bureaus, speak their minds, and ensure that they are properly implemented without hindrance so that anti-smuggling can make significant progress. This is what the chairman hopes for." Subsequently, Zou Lin delivered a speech on behalf of Minister Song Ziwen. Finally, refreshments were served and the meeting adjourned. Thereafter, a plenary session will be held every day from 2 p.m. onwards to discuss the issues. From the 4th to the 7th, a review meeting will be held every day from 9 a.m. to 12 p.m. to review various proposals. The plenary session will close at 5 p.m. on the 8th.

Most Favored Nation Treatment for Chinese Silk Exports to Egypt 121

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Replied

The Chamber of Commerce Relayed

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the silk industry stating that Chinese silk exports to Egypt were subject to higher tariffs due to the lack of a treaty. The Chamber of Commerce requested that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs expedite the signing of a treaty to remedy the situation. After investigation, it was determined that the Joint Business Association had previously requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to expedite the signing of a treaty regarding the heavy tariffs on Chinese tobacco exports to Egypt. It has now been learned that an agreement has been signed and exchanged, covering all Chinese exports to Egypt. Chinese silk should not be a concern. The General Chamber of Commerce forwarded a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requesting clarification. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs replied with a telegram stating that the interim trade measures between China and Egypt specified all Chinese products, not just tobacco. A transcript of the exchanged documents was sent to the Chamber of Commerce, which then forwarded it to the silk industry for their information.

Japanese Maritime Bureau Did Not Prohibit Chinese Ships from Carrying Goods to Japan 124

The Ministry of Transportation Informed the Shipping Association

The Shanghai Shipping Association previously received a letter from its member, Zhengji Company, stating that Chinese ships chartered by the company were planning to load goods in Dalian and transport them to Japan, but were suddenly prohibited by the Japanese Maritime Bureau. This not only crippled the business of Chinese ships but also intentionally infringed upon Chinese sovereignty. The association requested the Ministry of Transportation to intervene with the Japanese government through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protect sovereignty. It was previously reported that the request was approved. It is now known that the association has subsequently received instructions from the Ministry of Transportation, stating that after the Ministry of Foreign Affairs consulted with the Japanese government, the Japanese embassy replied that the Maritime Bureau had not taken any prohibitive action. The association has informed Zhengji Company accordingly. The instructions from the Ministry of Transportation and the attached original reply are as follows:

Ministry of Transportation Instruction No. 2311: Order to Implement Matters. Regarding the case of Chinese ships being prohibited from loading goods in Dalian by the Japanese Maritime Bureau, this association has repeatedly telegraphed the matter and consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to intervene with the Japanese side. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has approved the consultation and notified the case. Now, we have received a reply stating that the Japanese embassy has replied that the Maritime Bureau has not taken any prohibitive action, etc. The original reply is hereby copied and issued to the association for notification. This order.

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Document to the Ministry of Transportation Regarding the Prior Consultation: Regarding the case of the Chinese ship of Yingkou Overseas Trading Company being prohibited from loading goods in Dalian by the Maritime Bureau, the matter was previously submitted to the Japanese ambassador for investigation and a preliminary reply was sent. Now, the Japanese embassy replied, stating that the Chinese ship was a steamer belonging to the Beiyang Fleet and was entrusted to Zhengji Company for operation. At that time, the ship had been chartered by a Japanese merchant in Dalian. The Japanese merchant inquired with the Dalian Maritime Bureau about the procedures for the Chinese ship to transport coal to Japan. The Maritime Bureau kindly explained. Afterwards, it is unknown why the ship did not load goods and left the port. In fact, no prohibitive measures were taken, etc. Please note accordingly.

Important News from the Yangtze River Shipping Area 126

China Merchants Resumes Upper Yangtze Route. Since the implementation of the reorganization of China Merchants' Yangtze River shipping on July 1, progress has been gradually made. However, the incidents of leased ships and reduced schedules, followed by the assassination of Zhao Tieqiao, have greatly hampered business. The responsible person, Chief Li of the Business Section, is still striving to advance the original plan. From August 1, the Jiangjing, Jiangjing, Anjiang, Shunjiang, Xinjianguo, and Jianghua ships will be assigned to the 1st, 3rd, 4th, and 6th regular routes on the Yangtze River. In addition, the Hanyi route to the upper Yangtze River, which has been suspended for many years, will be officially restored starting from August 1. An agreement has been reached with the Transportation Department of the General Office to dispatch the returned Jiangyu, Jiangda, and Jiangtian ships to Hankou, Shashi, Yuezhou, and Yichang to compete with foreign merchants' ships on the upper Yangtze River route in order to recover lost profits.

Swire Adds Hulk in Hankou. British merchant Swire & Co. is renovating first-class new hulks in Hankou and Jiujiang to expand cargo transportation. The new hulk in Jiujiang was completed and towed away last month. The new hulk in Hankou, named "Ximi," has been built in Shanghai and has a very large capacity. Yesterday, the Yangtze River ship Wenzhou was ordered to tow it to Hankou for installation.

Marine Vessel Encountered Danger in Strong Wind 128

A Japanese ship drifted to Shanghai. The Sanyo Maru, a 4,360-ton ship of the Japanese Sanyo Steamship Company, loaded cargo in Hankou on July 27 and sailed to Qinhuangdao. When it reached the outer reaches of the Wusongkou, about 80 nautical miles from Shanghai, it encountered a strong wind. The engine and other machinery inside the ship were damaged by the wind and waves. The ship drifted on the sea for five days and nights. The shipowner telegraphed Japan for help. The company then sent the rescue ship Nasu Maru to tow it outside Wusong. It was originally intended to take it to Qinhuangdao to unload the cargo, but due to the difficulty of traveling due to the mechanical damage, it was towed to Shanghai. It has now arrived in Shanghai. The crew and sailors are all safe, but the machinery needs major repairs.

Sailor Fell into the Sea. The Daiyamaru, a river ship of the Japanese Postal Steamship Company, loaded cargo in Hankou on July 26 and sailed to Shanghai, and then exported to Yawata, Japan. Unexpectedly, the ship encountered a hurricane in the Yellow Sea. At that time, a sailor, a Japanese named Shen He Wufu, was working on the deck. Suddenly, a huge wave hit the sailor and knocked him into the sea. After stopping the ship, the crew sent a small sampan into the sea to rescue him in the raging waves, but there was no trace of him. It is presumed that he was swept away by the huge waves.

Guangli Has Not Been Towed Out. The China Merchants Bureau's Guangli ship ran aground on Glen Island in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Jiangyu went to tow it, but it was ineffective. It has not been rescued yet. The bureau has continued to send a tugboat to wait at the grounding site and will attempt to tow it again when the tide rises.

French Concession Extra Tax Reduced by One Li First 129

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession previously stated that the Public Concession had reduced the extra tax by two li from July 1 this year, but the French Concession had not announced the cancellation of the temporary two-li tax that was increased at the same time as the Public Concession. The association had repeatedly requested the French Municipal Council to cancel the tax to show public trust. The French Municipal Council replied to the Ratepayers' Association on the 30th of last month, agreeing to reduce the tax by one li first to comply with public opinion. The reply is translated as follows: (The following is a translation)

French Concession Municipal Council Official Letter No. 1570: Dear Sirs, The Municipal Committee of this Bureau has carefully considered the wishes expressed by your association on behalf of the Chinese ratepayers of the French Concession. On the other hand, it must also take into account the financial arrangements of this Bureau. Therefore, at the meeting held yesterday, it was resolved to reduce the housing tax by one li. This housing tax will be reduced to 13% from July 1 this year. The great talents of the members of your association have been fully revealed in several conversations, and the superintendent is deeply impressed that you have now achieved the above-mentioned resolution. A copy of the announcement of this Bureau that will be published in the newspapers (see the advertisement column of this newspaper) is enclosed for your review. As for the other items mentioned in your letter of July 23, they are currently being reviewed by our Consul General. Sincerely, Municipal Superintendent of the French Concession, Fan Erde, July 30.

Public Notice of the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession: Public Notice to the Chinese Ratepayers of the French Concession. Regarding the reduction of one li from July 1, those who have already paid can return to the Tax Office of the Municipal Council with their tax tickets to claim a refund, etc. It can be seen that the Municipal Council is trying its best to maintain its credibility within the constraints of the budget. Based on this fact, it can be inferred that the Municipal Council will not include the remaining one li of extra tax in next year's budget. In addition, the issue of increasing the number of Chinese directors is still being discussed. A further announcement will be made once a decision is made. Special Notice. Shanghai French Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association, July 31, Republic of China 19.

County District Requests Postponement of Grain Tax Collection 133

Difficult to Approve

The Minhang Hoxiangqiao area of Shanghai County was damaged by hail in the previous month. The county government sent personnel to conduct an on-site inspection. The heads of the townships in the first district reported the matter to the district, which then reported it to the county government, requesting a postponement of the collection of the winter grain tax for the 18th year. Yan, the county magistrate, instructed the county finance bureau to reply. The reply stated that the winter grain tax was about to end and was related to national revenue, so it was difficult to approve. The district head, Wu, has been instructed by the county government to instruct the township heads to separately investigate the damaged farmland, create a register, and report it to the county for submission to the provincial government for consideration during the autumn inspection.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance yesterday, requesting strict orders to exempt the tax on domestically produced soap, as the Zhejiang tax bureaus had reimposed the soap tax, which had been approved by the Ministry of Finance to be exempt. We recently received a reply stating

It has been found that all the 五洲[Five Continents], 固本[Fixed Foundation], 新愛[New Love], 華鼎[Hua Ding], 豐立[Feng Li], 大亨[Great Success], 公茂[Gong Mao], 華昌[Hua Chang], 永和[Yong He], 南陽[Nan Yang], and 新昌[Xin Chang] soap factories had been approved to pay tax in accordance with the regulations for machine-made foreign-style goods and should not be taxed repeatedly. Other factories without established cases are difficult to handle in the same way. In addition to instructing the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance and the Jiangxi Provincial Special Commissioner of Finance to comply separately, we are notifying you by telegram. The telegram stated that the ten soap factories had previously been approved to pay taxes in accordance with the regulations for machine-made foreign-style goods and should not be taxed repeatedly. Other factories without established cases are difficult to handle in the same way. In addition to instructing the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance and the Jiangxi Provincial Special Commissioner of Finance to comply separately, we are notifying you by telegram. The association immediately forwarded this to the ten soap factories for compliance. Now, Qixin Soap Factory states that after receiving the letter, a batch of soap was transported to Zhejiang, but the people in the tax bureau stated that they had not yet received instructions and still required the payment of tax before allowing the goods to pass. The Ministry of Finance's telegram was issued on the micro date, which was quite a while ago, and it has not yet been forwarded. In recent times, personnel handling tax matters often use the excuse that the order has not arrived to delay the process and still collect taxes, so although the government has good intentions to sympathize with domestically produced goods, merchants have not yet enjoyed the actual benefit of tax exemption. Municipal Government Approves the Cancellation of the Road Maintenance Donation Collected Concurrently with the Military Industrial Road 135

The Municipal Land Bureau stated that all transfer taxes and municipal administrative expenses collected concurrently with the issuance of contract papers are now unified in name and number as part of the unified revenue and expenditure of the municipal treasury. All scattered and miscellaneous donations collected according to old precedents have been cancelled. According to the precedent along the military industrial road, for every 100 yuan of contract price for construction and sale, a road maintenance donation of 5 yuan must be collected concurrently with the payment of the transfer tax to be used for the repair of the road. Now that other municipal roads have no special donations, the land along the military industrial road should not be treated differently. Therefore, the bureau submitted a request to the municipal government to approve the cancellation of the donation. It is reported that the municipal government has approved the cancellation of the collection from the 19th year.

The First Step to Remedy the High Gold and Low Silver Situation

Municipal Finance Bureau Rectifies Lane House Tax 137

Assessing Staff Should Pay Attention at All Times

Tang, the Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau, investigated and found that in various lanes and alleys of the city, some households not operating in storefronts were mistakenly assessed at the residential tax rate. This is inconsistent with the tax collection rules, and therefore requires rectification. He issued an order to various tax collection offices on the 28th of last month, stating that Article 12 of the city's house tax collection rules stipulates that houses in a storefront style but not used for business should be taxed as residential properties, while houses not in a storefront style but used for business should be taxed as commercial properties. Since the tax rates for commercial and residential properties are different, a clear and detailed investigation should be conducted to ensure compliance with the regulations and fairness. Last year, the bureau sent staff to investigate rent and conduct spot checks. Many discrepancies were corrected, but recently, it was discovered that in various lanes and alleys of the city, some houses not in a storefront style but used for business were still being taxed as residential properties. Therefore, a thorough inspection is necessary to rectify this situation. Considering that the tax collectors collect taxes door-to-door, it should not be difficult to distinguish between commercial and residential properties. It is hereby ordered that each collection office instruct its staff to conduct thorough inspections during tax collection and make corrections at any time, without concealment or favoritism. In the future, if any discrepancies in tax amounts are found, the staff member in charge will be punished for negligence. This order shall be complied with, in addition to separate instructions. At the same time, the bureau's investigation division is ordered to conduct strict and thorough inspections at all times.

Six Arrested in Chen Child Kidnapping Case 142

A Mr. Song Arrested in Yingchunfang

The Whereabouts of the Kidnapped Child Are Still Unknown

Chen, a four-year-old boy from Huzhou living at No. 2, Shihua Lane, Huanghe Road, French Concession, was kidnapped on the 20th of last month without a trace. At that time, because the child only had his grandmother and was the heir to several families, the family did not report to the police or announce the matter to the public in order to avoid the danger of the kidnappers killing the child. Unexpectedly, the kidnappers repeatedly sent letters demanding a ransom of 150,000 yuan. The first contact required a prepaid negotiation fee of 3,000 yuan. The child's family only has a widowed grandmother. Although the child's father once opened a foreign goods store and jewelry business across from the Grand Theatre in Japan, he actually had no savings. The kidnappers' demands were excessive and could not be met. The kidnappers sent another letter a few days ago instructing the family to send someone to a certain place in the Public Concession on August 1st (yesterday) to meet the kidnappers with four biscuit tins. The police detectives learned of this and immediately disguised themselves as hawkers and followed the person making contact. By the time they reached the destination, it was 8:30 PM. Three people approached the person to talk. The detectives rushed forward and arrested all three people. They were taken to the police station for interrogation. According to their confession, the mastermind of the case is a Mr. Gu from Yancheng, who is hiding at No. 309, Yingchunfang, Hubei Road. It was already 9:45 PM when the detectives, along with one of the arrested, went to the Gu residence and arrested a Mr. Song in the north wing of the house downstairs. He was taken to the Laozha Police Station. He was a very tall man, wearing a Western suit, about forty years old, with a small mustache. He claimed that he was currently working in a certain organization and had been living there for over a month. He claimed that the matter was a false accusation by his enemies. The police chief ordered his detention. Two more people were arrested one after another, but as of 1:00 AM this morning, the whereabouts of the kidnapped child were still unknown.

Three Men and Women Attempt Suicide in the Huangpu River, All Rescued 143

Su Xin, courtesy name Boying, from Hangzhou, has been unemployed for a long time.

He is 36 years old and a graduate of Yuxiu Middle School. He is skilled in small calligraphy and has a solid foundation in learning. He has served as a clerk in the Zhejiang Provincial Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau, the Zhejiang Industrial Hall, the Hang County Government Office, and the West Lake Exposition. When the exposition closed last year, Su also lost his job. He came to Shanghai in May to find a suitable position and temporarily lived with his brother-in-law, Wang Hanliang, in Hualong Lane, Hualong Road, French Concession. After two or three months, he could not find a suitable opportunity, so he pawned his clothes and spent his savings. He was looked down upon by others and had no face to stay at his brother-in-law's house. He recalled that his parents had passed away, and his wife had also died. He was alone and unlucky in Shanghai, so he had the idea of ending his life. At around 7:00 PM the night before, he went to the Xinkang Wharf on Hankou Road and boarded the No. 4 ferry. When the ferry reached the middle of the river, he jumped into the river when people were not paying attention. Fortunately, the old captain Zhang Ah'er was quick and bravely rescued him, preventing him from drowning. He was sent to the water police station, and the police chief ordered him to be helped after learning the details. In a moment of anger, a middle-aged woman suddenly jumped into the Huangpu River at the Jinliyuan Wharf of the China Merchants Bureau at around 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon. The body sank and then floated up again. Fortunately, She Jincai, an inspector from the bureau, was patrolling the riverbank in a boat and immediately rescued her when he saw her. Because she had swallowed too much water, she was unconscious. Artificial respiration was used to gradually revive her. The water police station sent police to take her to the police station and ordered Detective Huang Songsheng to send her to Renji Hospital for diagnosis to ensure that she was not in danger before returning to the police station. According to her confession, she is surnamed Lu, named Li, 35 years old, from Hubei, and lives at No. 11, a certain lane, Route du Père Froc, French Concession. Her husband's name is Lu Shaoqing, who is a general manager. He has been unemployed for more than three months. She has two daughters. The eldest daughter, Yu Zhen, is 17 years old and married Zhou Genbao, who runs a fruit stall on Route du Père Froc, in February last year. The younger daughter, Meizhen, is not yet engaged. Today, her husband's older brother (uncle) came to visit. Because she was feeling unwell, she asked Meizhen to cook rice, but it was not to her liking, which angered her husband, who scolded her and her daughter. In a moment of anger, she was willing to die. The police chief ordered the detective to inform her family to come to the police station to claim Li.

Pessimism About Life At around 9:00 AM yesterday, a 144

middle-aged woman wearing a coarse rice-colored linen shirt, solid-colored foreign yarn trousers, gold hoop earrings, and a hair bun hired a ferry from Jiangtian Wharf on the 16th pier to cross the Huangpu River. When the ferry approached the Bund of the Hongsheng Wharf in Pudong Lannidu, the woman suddenly jumped into the river and committed suicide. Fortunately, the tide was rising at this time, and her body floated on the surface of the water. She was rescued by the boatman and sent to the police station of the Third District of the Public Security Bureau. According to the woman's confession, her name is Long Wang, 39 years old, from Nanjing. When asked about her detailed address and the reason for her suicide, she refused to tell the truth. After repeated questioning, she finally said that she lost her husband at the age of 32 and had no children. She then came to Shanghai and lived in her mother's house, that is, No. 15, Lane 49, Jiangbian Wharf, Gaochang Temple, making a living by sewing. She has an older brother named Wang Disheng, who works as a mechanic in the artillery factory there. She thought that life in this world was meaningless, so she embraced pessimism and jumped into the river to end her remaining life. The district chief checked the confession and planned to order her brother to come and claim her. The woman firmly refused, so he prepared a document in the afternoon and transferred her to the Public Security Bureau for disposal.

Dong denied being the owner of the store, claiming to be a shop assistant with a monthly salary of 20 yuan who had only been hired on July 10th. The store wanted him to pay a deposit of 50 yuan, so he resigned. He claimed that the handgun in his house was deposited by Mr. Liu, the former district chief of the Third District of Pudong, and that it was a rusted gun. Liu had already left to seek employment. He hired Lawyer Jiang Baoli to defend him. Judge Feng ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for further questioning.

○ Zhou Family Property Dispute Case: Deadline for Partition. Jinmei, the 21-year-old daughter of Zhou Zhou, a widow in the Zhou family in Yangshupu, recently became intimate with Kun Sheng, a member of the clan, and they appeared to be husband and wife. Her mother not only did not restrain them but also considered Kun Sheng as a future son-in-law. This angered Zhou Ziqi, the widow’s second uncle, and Zhou Fubao, the son of the deceased third uncle, who often argued with the Zhou Zhou mother and daughter, leading to separation and eventually fighting. The widow hired Lawyer E Sen to accuse Zhou Ziqi and his nephew of illegally detaining property and causing injury. The Special District Local Court had summoned them for questioning, as reported in this newspaper. The hearing continued yesterday morning, with the defendants also hiring Lawyer Ye Fukan for defense. The plaintiff stated that if the defendants could fairly distribute the family property, they would withdraw the case. Judge Cheng asked if the defendant did in fact have addictions because the plaintiff's complaint included statements about Ziqi not engaging in proper business, being addicted to opium, and being fond of gambling. The defendant vehemently denied it. The court advised them to divide the family property fairly to avoid prolonged litigation. Zhou Ziqi requested two months, but Judge Cheng believed that dividing the assets worth tens of thousands of yuan should not take that long, indicating an intention to delay. He set a deadline of seven days, which the defendant agreed to. Judge Cheng further instructed the plaintiff that if the property partition was completed, they should submit a written withdrawal of the lawsuit. The hearing was adjourned for seven days.

Inspecting Pedestrians

Bullet Enters Stone Crevice

Zhang Guifang, a patrol officer from the First Precinct of the Fourth District of Zhabei, was inspecting pedestrians alongside Officer Ye Shouchun near the railway overpass yesterday. Fortunately, the muzzle was pointing downwards, and the bullet entered a crack in the stone, avoiding a tragic incident. At that time, pedestrians were constantly passing by. No Extortion of "Dry Foot Money" Allowed 158

Public Notice from the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus: Ships from the countryside arriving at the wharves along the Huangpu River are mainly used for transporting goods. However, upon arrival, porters swarm the ships, forcibly carrying goods regardless of the owner and extorting tips, which is extremely abhorrent. The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and Public Security Bureau have issued a notice stating that Xing Zhigang, a representative of ships from Pudong, reported that porters led by Xi Akun at the Nanhuiguan Wharf and Zhang Shunhe at the Wanyu Wharf to Yongsheng Wharf, would swarm the ships upon arrival, forcibly carry goods, and extort tips. Those who carried their own goods were also forced to pay "dry foot money" and "wharf money." If their demands were not met, they would detain the goods and act violently. The bureaus ordered the First Sub-bureau of the First District and the Water Patrol Team to investigate. The investigation confirmed that the porters were indeed demanding "dry foot money," forcibly obstructing transportation, and extorting labor fees. In addition to ordering the Water Patrol Team to work with the First Sub-bureau of the First District to bring the porters, as well as the plaintiff Xing Zhigang and witnesses Yang Guanlin and Zhou Jinwen, to the bureau for questioning as a warning, a joint public notice was issued to inform merchants and ship owners that if any porters were found extorting or causing disturbances, they should be immediately handed over to the Water Patrol Team or the relevant district sub-bureau to be transferred to the bureau for legal action.

Refusing to Pay for Teapot Repair

Blaming Wife, Pushing Her to Death

Sheng Changfu, 35, who lives in Wusong and makes a living by rowing boats, is known for his rudeness and fondness for alcohol, being drunk every day. Around 7:00 PM the night before last, Sheng Changfu, again drunk, went to Liu Yongchang's copper and tin shop on Tongxing Road in Wusong to retrieve a teapot he had entrusted to the shop for repair during the day. He refused to pay for the repair as it had not been a year since the purchase. His tone was aggressive. The shop assistant, seeing that he was drunk and unreasonable, did not argue with him. At this time, Sheng Changfu's wife, Han, was also present and, seeing the situation, feared that her husband would cause trouble due to his drunkenness. She stepped forward to persuade him to go home. Unexpectedly, Sheng Changfu not only refused to listen but turned his anger on his wife, pushing Han with great force. She fell to the ground and died instantly. A crowd gathered. The patrol police arrived and arrested Sheng Changfu, taking him to the First Sub-bureau of the Seventh District for questioning.

Central Bank Inspection Report 164

Central Bank's 61st Inspection Report on Issuance Reserves: In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of convertible banknotes by this bank. The 61st inspection was conducted at the issuing bureau of this bank on July 31, 1920. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: Total issuance of convertible banknotes: 16,779,548 silver dollars, including 15,763,841 silver dollar notes and 1,015,707 yuan of subsidiary currency notes. Total convertible banknote reserve funds: 16,779,548 silver dollars, including 14,085,249.60 silver dollars in cash reserve. The cash reserve includes 11,054,522.73 silver dollars stored in this bank's issuing vault, 1,243,185.14 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,787,541.73 silver dollars deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve is converted to 2,694,298.40 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. July 31, 1920. Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank: Li Fuxun. Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Lin Jilong.

Jiang Xiaojian's Letter to Various Institutions 175

Regarding the Statue of Dr. Sun Yat-sen at the North Railway Station

Concerning the matter of constructing a statue of Dr. Sun Yat-sen at the North Railway Station with donations from various sectors, more than a month has passed since the bidding process began, and no decision has been made regarding whose design to use or who should undertake the construction. The artist Mr. Jiang Xiaojian has some suggestions for the statue construction standing committee. Yesterday, he sent letters to five institutions, namely the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Government, the Garrison Headquarters, the Two Roads Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce (the five standing committee members). The letter stated: "Regarding the preparatory committee for the construction of the statue by various sectors, the standing committee formed by the aforementioned five institutions is responsible for all aspects of the bidding and construction. Mr. Jiang Xiaojian believes that creating a statue is a unique art form, quite different from ordinary construction projects where drawings are prepared before bidding. Therefore, I have some doubts about the above method. However, due to the urgency of time, I only stated in the specifications that the stone base could be contracted to others, and the price for the stone base was not definitely confirmed. I believe that Dr. Sun Yat-sen is our founding father, illustrious for all ages. Now, constructing a statue in Shanghai concerns the view of both Chinese and foreigners, and it must be done with special care. The reason why I, Mr. Jiang Xiaojian, am willing to devote my skills to undertake this task is precisely for this reason. The bidding results have not yet been announced, but based on my personal experience, I deeply feel that there are several major errors that could lead to unfavorable outcomes. For example, for such a specialized art, from bidding to review, people with knowledge and expertise in this field must be appointed to ensure fairness and prudence. However, the representatives appointed by the various institutions are rashly taking charge of the matter, leading to significant errors in the bidding process. What are these errors? The failure to prohibit the listing of names on the drawings is one of them. It is unprecedented in bidding practice to allow names to be listed on the drawings. The failure to prohibit this has led to the reviewers knowing whose drawings belong to whom from the very beginning, causing external discussions and the inability of the reviewers to reach a consensus after months of deliberation. This is the first error. Secondly, none of the reviewers are art experts, so it is unclear what criteria they are using to judge. If the construction is carried out according to the drawings and cannot be applied, or if modifications are proposed but specialists cannot implement them, who will be responsible? Furthermore, Mr. Wang, a committee member from the Roads Bureau, even invited Mr. Jiang Xiaojian to the bureau in a private capacity to discuss modifying the drawings and the possibility of collaborating with another bidder, Mr. Zhang Chenbo, but did not invite Mr. Zhang to discuss the matter together in person. This attitude is also very perplexing. I hereby formally declare that the construction of the statue at the North Railway Station must be carried out in accordance with the following procedures to be appropriate: (1) It is extremely difficult to assess the merits of the art of statue construction based on flat drawings. Experts should carefully examine whether the design is in the Chinese style and investigate the artist's past achievements and reputation. (2) The main procedure for making the statue is to create a clay model. Therefore, it is particularly important to examine the artist's past achievements to see if they have artistic value and to investigate whether the equipment in their bronze casting workshop is suitable for statue making. The casting work cannot be done in ordinary sand casting workshops. (3) When reviewing the drawings, attention should be paid to the fact that the statue is the main element, and the stone base is secondary. If there are drawings for the stone base, any stonemason can build it, but the statue cannot be made by anyone who does not have extensive statue-making experience. Otherwise, it will lead to the inappropriateness of the secondary element overshadowing the main one. All of the above points are matters that should be handled. Perhaps all the previously submitted bids should be canceled and experts' designs should be solicited from home and abroad to ensure prudence. Because for such an important project, it is difficult to make a decision by only comparing two or three people. I have heard that the standing committee's review criteria are contrary to this. Although the review results are not yet known, the identities of the reviewers and the review methods already suggest that they cannot produce good results. Therefore, regardless of whether my designs are selected or rejected, I cannot agree and believe that I have the right to insist on the above points based on my artistic standing. Therefore, I dare to write this letter, requesting attention and hoping for a response."

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter, Hai Ke 176

Wife A: I think opening a store is an interesting thing. I really want to open a small grocery store and have fun. What do you want to open, Wife B?

Wife B: Every night, after my husband falls asleep, I open his wallet and secretly hide one or two banknotes. During the day, I open his letters to see if there are any love letters.

Husband: Our cook is working very hard today. This bowl of noodles tastes good.

Wife: This is what she made for the milkman. But this morning, they somehow had a quarrel, so this bowl of noodles is being enjoyed by you.

Mother: Child, the dormitory supervisor at school wrote a letter asking why you haven't been to school for three days. Go quickly.

Child: I really don't understand what they mean. There are already many children like me at school. Why do they insist that I go?

A: Old Bing's temper couldn't be stranger. He is usually comfortable and has no worries, but he insists on looking for trouble himself.

B: Then why doesn't he get married?

Husband: New clothes, new clothes, new clothes! You always pester me with this. Besides new clothes, don't you have any other thoughts?

Wife: I do, but I don't know if you're willing. I also want a pair of pearl earrings and a diamond ring.

A Short Stay at Moganshan (I), Jingbo 177

Everyone knows that Qingdao, Mount Lu, Beidaihe, and Moganshan are all places where one can escape the summer heat, cleanse their minds, and avoid worldly customs. People in the south who fear the hardship of travel and want convenient transportation often go to Qingdao or Moganshan. In Qingdao, the Dalian steamer departs from Shanghai and arrives the next day. The sea breeze is pleasant, and the scenery is captivating, making it a delightful place. However, I believe that when we escape the summer heat, we should seek a spacious place, preferably with high mountains. Secondly, when living leisurely during the summer, we should seek tranquility. Although we don't necessarily need to be isolated from the world, we should try to stay away from the hustle and bustle, and the food and drink we need should be readily available. Other amenities, such as ball games and swimming facilities, should also be available. In general, should we not take a trip to Moganshan?

In the past, to climb the mountain from Shanghai, one had to depart early in the morning, transfer to a small boat at Gongchen Bridge, and arrive at Sanqiaopu in the evening. Then, one would change to a sedan chair to climb the mountain, and it would already be night. It took more than twelve hours. Although transportation was considered convenient, the day-long boat and car ride was exhausting. Since the completion of the highway, the journey from Hubin to Yucun at the foot of the mountain is over a hundred miles, and hiring a car only takes an hour and a half to reach directly. If you get off at the city station, it is even faster to take a car. In terms of time, it never takes more than eight hours from Shanghai to the top of the mountain. When the joint passenger ticket and transportation are completed in the future, transportation will become even more convenient, and the Ninghang Highway has also been tested. There will be endless scenery on Moganshan.

I went to Hangzhou this time, stayed overnight, and climbed the mountain early in the morning. At six o'clock, the car was already waiting at the door of the hotel, and the ride was very smooth. The lotus flowers in the lake were in full bloom, with green leaves and red skirts stretching as far as the eye could see. After passing Xiaoche Station, the speed of the car increased, and the beauty of the Zhejiang Province highway was especially admirable. The highway bureau has been operating for years, and the value is considerable. Opening up the wilderness and making a flat road is like grinding a whetstone, so there is no bumpy ride. Along the way, distant peaks stand tall, mountains surround and embrace, and lush forests and tall bamboos make the sound of water gurgling. The beauty of the scenery is hard to describe.

Recording the Dowry of Hangzhou Municipal Government 178

The site of the Hangzhou Municipal Government is the former ancestral hall of Yang Shandeh, the late Zhejiang Governor. After the National Revolutionary Army settled in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, it was confiscated by the Zhejiang Provincial Government and allocated as the site of the Hangzhou Municipal Government.

The Giant Flies of Lanfeng, Yu Ying

It is said that at the beginning of this month, countless giant flies suddenly appeared in the sky over Lanfeng City. Their bodies were as large as bees, butterflies, and locusts. The local people were shocked and retreated in fear, afraid of being harmed by them. They dared not sleep in the open air even in the hot weather. It is said that there have never been such giant flies in Lanfeng before. Similar events have also occurred in neighboring counties, which is also strange.

When it was confiscated, the full dowry of Yang Shandeh's daughter-in-law was also inside. At the beginning of his term, former Mayor Zhou Xiangxian saw that the dowry was too good and was being moved and used by servants in the city, which would inevitably lead to damage. Therefore, he removed a room, sealed it, and preserved it. At that time, some government officials proposed to auction off the dowry and use the proceeds for charitable purposes or allocate them as start-up funds for a certain school as a memorial and to avoid decay. However, Zhou rejected all of these proposals. As a result, this beautiful dowry was temporarily unharmed and spared from being scattered among the people.

Some commentators said that Zhou's actions were unable to make use of waste and only maintained the name of preservation, which was not what a political economist should do. Others said that Zhou was able to think big and that the reason why he insisted on preserving it was to warn government officials against corruption, not to seek a few thousand taels of silver. This is exactly what a political economist should do.

Now, Cai Zengji has replaced Zhou as the head of the Hangzhou Municipal Government. I wonder if he has any plans for this dowry issue.

Fifty-Two Ears in a Polish Train, Lu Bing 180

The police were extremely busy

The result was a great disappointment

According to a European dispatch this month, people all over Poland read a strange case in the morning newspaper: a package abandoned by passengers was found on a train from Wasaton to Lotz. When the police at the station opened it, they found fifty-two human ears inside, each carefully wrapped in cotton wool, indicating that the perpetrator was extremely careful with them. The ears seemed to be freshly cut, so the police initially reported that the incident occurred no more than a few hours before it was discovered. The matter spread far and wide, and everyone who knew about it was amazed. However, when the police investigated, they found that all the residents of Poland still had both ears and none were missing. Therefore, suspicions arose, and it was regarded as a strange case. Even after expert research, opinions differed, and no definite conclusion was reached. Before long, someone went to the police headquarters to request the return of the lost human ears. According to his proof, he was a dissection instructor, and the contents of the package were indeed the original items, but the ears were made of rubber and looked exactly like real ones. The cloud of suspicion was suddenly dispelled, making it a very interesting story.

I have longed for West Lake for ten years, and now my wish has finally come true. It cannot be said that I have no connection with the beauty of West Lake. Awakening from an early dream, the sunlight breaks through the window and enters. Pushing back the quilt, I look down and see green mountains and blue pools, all within reach. I don't know where the fragrance comes from, but I feel a refreshing fragrance that invigorates my spirit. The white clouds in front of my eyes sometimes rise and fall leisurely. Looking north, my parents' house is far away in Jimen. I recall the kind instructions when I returned south at the beginning of summer, which seem like yesterday. Now, I have abandoned myself and abruptly become eternally separated. Countless thoughts surge in my chest like wind-swept clouds. Heart Shadows of a Journey to the East (II)(X) 182

(X)(6) The Scandal of the Philippine Athletes

The scandal of the Philippine athletes, which was once a sensation, has been recorded in the newspapers in Shanghai, but the details are not clear. The tabloids have added many unfounded words, calling it a "beauty trap" by the Japanese, which is far from the truth. The reporter saw and heard more accurate information in Japan, so I am recording it here. The Japan Youth Center, where the athletes of the three countries were staying together, is originally a club for young students. Usually, there are female students' figures. Since the opening of the conference, female students have come in groups of hundreds to admire the prestige of the Chinese and Philippine athletes. Therefore, the Youth Center was filled with a crowd of females, adding a lot of color. Since the tide of autographs, even more people came, with the majority of those surrounding the athletes being the women's army, accounting for seven or eight out of ten. Most of the Chinese and Philippine athletes do not know Japanese, and the female students only know a little English. The two sides gesture and laugh. The athletes are not all wood and stone, and they are also happy to socialize. The female students' psychology of worshiping sports heroes is even stronger than that of ordinary Japanese women, because they completely take physique as the goal of beauty. Therefore, the Philippine athletes were the first to be selected. Initially, many Chinese athletes also interacted with female students, but due to the strict management and the weakness of their physique, it was only a matter of ethics and there was no further love affair. From May 27th, the Philippine athletes and female students had a deeper understanding and advanced to the second stage of work. Every evening when the sun sets, pairs of Philippine athletes and female students can be seen walking under the trees around the Outer Garden of the Shrine, arm in arm and whispering to each other, and cafes are the only place for them to talk about love. On the evening of May 29th, it was completely mature and an international love affair occurred. Initially, the Japanese police, in view of the licentious behavior of the female students in recent days and the intimacy with the Philippine athletes, secretly ordered the Japanese police to pay special attention. Around 1:00 a.m. on the 29th, a Philippine athlete and a female student were discovered by the police in a secluded place in the woods near the track and field and taken into the police station. At the same time, more than a dozen Philippine athletes and Japanese women with improper behavior in the Outer Garden were also detained. Because it was an international matter, they were slightly condemned and released. The next day, the Tokyo Nichinichi Shimbun published the process of the love affair with a large headline, attacking the police station for failing to prevent it in advance and disrespecting the dignity of international competition. However, the Filipinos did not understand Japanese, so even though the city was full of news, they were still calm because they did not read newspapers, and their love continued as usual without being hit much. Therefore, on the evening of the same day, more than a dozen men and women were again inspected in the hotels and cafes near the shrine, and the Philippine delegation went to the police station to bail them out. The love affair was thus concluded. The Japanese police, under attack from public opinion, tried their best to investigate the facts. On the 30th, more than 60 female students were interrogated by the police. In addition, on February 2nd, the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department summoned two students from a girls' school in Kujiki Ward, a 15-year-old, for detailed interrogation. It was heard that these two students, under the inducement of graduates, met three Philippine athletes staying at the Youth Center at the baseball field in the Outer Garden of the Shrine on the night of the 30th. Suppressing my grief, the waiter advanced my meal, so I called for wine and drank it alone. The wine entered my sorrowful heart, and the sorrow grew even stronger. I changed clothes and went to the lakeside, ordering a boat to linger in the middle of the stream as if sitting in heaven. The gentle breeze slightly dispelled my worries. Crossing the West Lake Bridge, I abandoned the boat and landed, walking and stopping until I reached the tomb of Master Manshu. I admired the Master's spirit across thousands of miles and paid my respects. Suddenly, I remembered the Master's poem, "Do not ask about life and death, just let the clouds and water flow, a lonely monk. Endlessly laughing wildly, endlessly crying, even if there is joy, it is already like ice." Thinking of the latter two lines is like a true portrait of me today, and my chronic illness is severe, and there is no way to escape Zen. The feeling of hidden pain is even more difficult to express. At times, the profuse flowers brush the wind, and pieces whirl and dance on my sleeves, seeming to love and pity my lonely figure, as if they can understand my words. I gathered all the fallen flowers and kissed them frequently, and then I regretted that the flowers may be unintentional, but I suddenly fell into a demonic obstacle. However, my nature is like this, and I am often teased without realizing it. Everyone calls me foolish and ignorant of the world. Alas, what is the world like, what is foolishness like? I truly know my own foolishness, but I cannot bear to hide my foolishness and pretend to be different from the world. As I walked and thought, I unknowingly reached Liu Zhuang for a short rest. I gently shook the oars and said to seek the Three Pools. Suddenly, the bell rang at sunset, and a dim smoke enveloped me. I suddenly felt like I was in Hua Xu, riding a dragon and carrying a cloud banner. The Qing Dynasty suddenly opened, and the Heavenly Emperor welcomed me. I stepped into the palace and saw that the walls were hung with curved jade and the room was brightly lit. The music master played the Dalu for me, and the beautiful women danced the rainbow dress for me. My eyes were dazzled and my spirit was confused. I was extremely happy and woke up. The tide crashed against each other, and the oars responded to each other. My mood was not happy. I looked up to the sky and sang loudly. The song said, "Xi He suddenly does not stay, stealing the world, where to seek? My body is weak, and death is not enough to atone for my sins. I look back at the vastness, why do I create resentment? (First verse) The profuse flowers drift in the wind, and all things grow sadly. Do not be sad about life and death. I delight in the stream and whistle. Who finishes the edge of the lake?"

Warm Whispers of the Heart (II)(IV)(VI) 183

Episode 13: Who Unintentionally Plants Blessings and Gains a Diamond Ring? This is the Fate, Deliberately Singing a Gold Thread Song

It turned out that the second prize that Zuo Shichen won today was a diamond ring, a pair of bracelet watches, two silver powder cases, and three gold buttons. Everyone heard that Zuo Shichen got a diamond ring, which can be regarded as a rare event. In fact, just saying the three words "diamond" has different sizes. The large ones are as big as a steel ball, worth hundreds of thousands of gold, or even millions of gold. Some come from deep palaces, and some come from private collections in mansions. The small ones, as fine as sand, are also diamonds and cannot be generalized. However, small diamonds are often only used as auxiliary products and cannot stand alone. A diamond that stands alone is called a "single stone" and naturally has its qualifications. The one that Zuo Shichen got is also a single stone ring. People were even more excited when they heard about it. In fact, although it is a single stone, it is quite small, but under the myriad lights like stars, it can also sparkle. No one knows which lady in the boudoir gave this universal garden tour's blessing ticket as a prize. No one knows on whose slender spring onion-like finger this ring was once worn, or what kind of legendary fact occurred on this ring. These small diamond rings are insignificant. If it is a large diamond in Shanghai, it is a demon in women's society. Often, a beautiful girl loses her chastity because of it. Often, a small family's daughter is so envious of this shiny little thing that she even falls to the point of drinking her hatred for life, or even dying of illness or committing suicide. It is simply commonplace and not worth mentioning. In fact, what is so great about wearing a ring on a finger and two diamonds dangling on the ears? Does it have infinite power to collect a vain heart? Those women with weak knowledge, even if it is a rare treasure, are not brought to life and not taken to death. Why fight for chastity and life? There are many such tragic events in Zuo Shichen's record. Now he also has a small one, which can be regarded as a microcosm. Looking at that pair of watches, you can think that this is the ancestor of the current popular watches. Originally, it suddenly became popular to wear the watch on the hand. There is a process of transformation, and this trace is the bracelet watch. Because the time watches have always been placed in the pocket, and to see the time, you take it out of the pocket. It can also be considered very convenient. But later, as European and American culture advanced, it became more and more troublesome to use hands. The time watch placed in the pocket must at least free up one hand to take out the watch, and sometimes both hands are used, such as opening airplanes, driving cars, and various machines. If you want to see what time it is and use one hand to take out the watch, it means that this one hand must temporarily stop efficiency. With a watch, the two hands can still work, and it can report to you what time it is on the wrist. This is how convenient it is.

The Flourishing Yarn Market 189

The public's eye is watching to see if 60 taels can be achieved.

The yarn market is very firm and sales are brisk. Buyers have a strong bullish attitude and most are aiming to see a price of 60 taels. The current autumn season's spot sales are continuous and distant prices reaching 60 taels is also to be expected. However, each factory still has inventory, but coarse yarn is tighter. 16-count and 20-count yarn sales are increasingly slow. Japanese yarn inventory is drier due to more purchases from various gangs. The yarn market currently has this sales activity, of course, cannot be bearish and the pulling force of buyers is therefore stronger.

The Tranquil Cotton Market 190

American cotton trends are mediocre. The local cotton market is still firm because the new cotton season is still early and the weather is sometimes cloudy and sometimes sunny and there may be storms. Bullish companies see the environment in August as bad and spot sales are not moving. Distant months are being absorbed, so the new cotton market is slightly firm. However, the Japanese trading company Toyo Cotton Mill is shorting on the rise because American cotton is not good. At present, the reports from various villages are good and it is still difficult to predict. It is heard that Chen Yin cotton from the Shanghai Japanese yarn factory can be used until the end of the Gregorian calendar year, so spot cotton transactions have been hit hard.

North China's New Cotton Grows Well 191

Tianjin News: Cotton production in North China is progressing smoothly. The situation in various producing areas is briefly recorded as follows: (1) West River Cotton: Due to rainfall in the producing areas, planting is slightly earlier or later. According to the current situation, it is estimated that it is about 80% of the normal year. If the weather is good in the future, it can increase by 30-40% compared to last year. American cotton producing areas such as Ningpu, Zhao County, and Pu County have expanded by about 20% compared to last year due to higher market prices. Cotton seedlings in Gaoyang, Boye, Qizhou, Rongcheng, Wanman, and Dingzhou are growing well. The Fuyang River Basin is not very good due to the uncoordinated irrigation system. (2) Yu River Cotton: The cotton field area has increased by about 15% compared to last year. American cotton has also increased and is growing well. The harvest is estimated to be about 80%. (3) Xiaoji Cotton: Some areas were initially affected by rain, but later the weather was smooth and the development was good. It can increase by 20% compared to last year. (4) Shanxi Cotton: The cotton planting area has increased by about 20%. The weather is suitable and the growth is good. It is estimated that the harvest is over 80%.

Grain and Foreign Rice Rise in the Morning, Fall in the Evening 194

Yesterday morning, foreign rice sales were very good. Innerland and Yantai gangs had a few social transactions. With more transactions, the market was lively. In the afternoon, a new shipment of cheap foreign rice arrived, about 20,000 bags. Although the delivery of previously ordered goods was completed early, there was still a considerable amount of goods that were fixed at a cheap price. Therefore, people's hearts tended to decline. Local rice dealers' appetite was also weak. All rice prices returned to around a small jiao. The total market transaction volume was 2,000 bags of Saigon Grade 1 rice at 16 yuan 5 jiao 7 fen, 2,000 bags of small crushed rice at 14 yuan 9 jiao, 500 bags of red small crushed rice at 12 yuan 7 jiao, 3,000 bags of large crushed rice at 12 yuan 7 jiao, and 500 bags of Min Dang rice at 14 yuan 9 jiao. The rough rice transaction volume was 3,500 bags of small crushed rough rice at 12 yuan and 1,000 bags of Xu Ye rough rice at 13 yuan and a half, according to the grade.

Market After Flour Tended Upward 195

The rumors say that the Tianjin goods are being loaded.

Yesterday morning, the flour market was suddenly hit by a huge shock. The price of foreign wheat was reported to have fallen by 8-9 jiao to 1.34 yuan the day before. Yesterday, the report was that it had risen by 3-4 jiao. Furthermore, the delivery warehouse receipts for the upper months were not taken by the buyers, but were hoarded by powerful people. Foreign firm brokers also came to sell foreign flour, offering a price of 3.8 yuan. The environment was not good and sales were not moving. Therefore, people's hearts were very nervous. After the opening price, they fell wildly, especially the selling sentiment in the distant months, such as September to November, which fell by 2 liang 4 qian and a half. January was the first time it opened and fell to 2 liang 4 qian 5 fen 2 li and a half. It can be seen that the falling trend was very fierce. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, people's hearts were suddenly excited. There were rumors that the spot goods at the Tianjin port could be loaded, which made the Tianjin and Yingkou gangs suddenly eager for the near and distant months, and people's hearts were encouraged by it. Therefore, the opening price rebounded step by step. If this statement is true, then the later step can be temporarily seen as stable and firm. As a result, the current month was 0.075 better than the previous month, September was 0.05 better, October and November were unchanged, December was 0.025 better, and January was 0.012 better than the morning.

Forward Wheat Market Follows Flour Market to Rebound 196

Yesterday, the forward wheat market showed an initial sluggishness followed by stability in the afternoon. At the beginning of the opening in the morning, the market was initially small for each month because the foreign wheat quotations were falling sharply, and it was once as small as 4 taels 7 qian 3 fen. However, it quickly recovered as the buying sentiment was good, and all months saw a rebound. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, people's hearts had become stable, and the trend was also stable and firm because the forward flour rebounded and there were rumors that the Tianjin gang had moved. As a result, August was 0.02 smaller than the previous month, September was 0.03 smaller, October was 0.01 smaller, November was unchanged, December was 0.01 better, and January initially opened at 4 taels 9 qian 2 fen and later was 0.02 better. Because the factory's appetite was weakening and the standards were unstable, spot wheat prices were smaller at all levels by 0.03-0.04, but the prices in the interior were not very low, and it is feared that the arrival of goods will become scarce. 5,000 bags of Chen wheat from Xuzhou, Taierzhuang, Yaowan, Tongzhou, Xinyang, and Hankou were opened and taken away by Fuxin.

Raw Silk and Tea: New York Silk Inventory Reaches 90,000 Bales, Market Weak 197

New York Market: Due to the unusually hot weather this year, silk mills have uniformly stopped for summer vacation. Recently, the heat has risen again and the factories have not yet reopened. Raw silk consumption has decreased sharply. Imports of Chinese and Japanese raw silk have not been weak, and the inventory of silk has increased. The city has a total of 89,680 bales of Chinese, Japanese, Italian, and French raw silk, which is sufficient for two months of demand.

Silk Market Tends to Be Quiet 198

Yesterday, the local foreign firm silk market was sluggish because New York silk sales were not rising, French sales were also limited, and the opening prices were still low. Because Chinese silk merchants felt that the losses were too great, they were reluctant to sell. Yesterday, only Lianna and others bought 20 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, Dachang bought 20 bales of yellow factory silk, and Samsung bought 12 bales of yellow coarse silk at stable prices.

Business News

The National Commercial Bank declares that its savings department, in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, has allocated separate funds to handle various savings deposits, striving for utmost prudence. Therefore, over the past three years, the total savings amount in all branches has reached over one million yuan, demonstrating public trust. Now, to ensure depositors understand the stability of their deposits, the bank has completely separated the accounting of the savings department. All income and expenditure accounts of the department will be audited by accountants quarterly, and depositors are welcome to inspect the liquidation. The results will be announced in the newspaper to demonstrate credibility. This truly sets a new record for savings banks in Shanghai.

Zhenhua Garden on Avenue Edward VII declares that its Tianxi brand chicken extract soy sauce essence and various health juice sauces, color national product paints, etc., have been well-received by the public since their release. It uses the latest scientific methods to refine pure juice from beans and wheat and incorporates various nourishing ingredients such as chicken extract as the main body. It is truly an essential item for healthy cooking. Therefore, people from all walks of life with some scientific knowledge praise it endlessly and are happy to purchase it.
